7
Magnetic Excitations in Overdoped BaFe2−xNixAs2
Figure7.14b summarize the doping and energy dependence of the magnetic cor-
relation length (ξ) along [1, K] direction. For BaFe2As2, the correlation lengthes
for low energy spin waves are relatively large. While for the x = 0.096, 0.15, 0.18
and 0.3 samples, the correlation lengthes of the high energy magnetic excitations are
similar and small (∼10 Å), indicating that they are diffusive paramagnons, similar
to the paramagnons in curpates [14, 15].
7.3
Summary
In conclusion, we have carried out inelastic neutron scattering studies on the dop-
ing dependence of the magnetic excitations in overdoped BaFe2−xNixAs2, with
x = 0.15, 0.18 and 0.3. The spin resonance mode decreases in intensity and energy
with increasing doping in the overdoped regime. This trend consistent with the doping
evolution of superconductivity (Tc and superﬂuid density) and thereby demonstrates
the importance of the low-energy magnetic excitations induced by interband scatter-
ing of the itinerant electrons. While the low-energy magnetic excitations undergo sig-
niﬁcant evolution with electron doping, the high-energy magnetic excitations (> 80
meV) change less in spectral weight and dispersion, suggesting that the interacting
local moments persist through the whole superconducting dome. This unconven-
tional paramagnetic state hosting well deﬁned exchange couplings (J) is a matrix
fortheemergenceofsuperconductivityand J isanessentialinteractionfordrivingthe
superconducting pairing. Therefore, the itinerant electron-spin excitation coupling
through J could be essential for driving the superconductivity.

Chapter 8
Summary and Outlook
We have performed detailed studies on the phase diagram and magnetic excitations
of BaFe2−xNixAs2 using neutron and x-ray scattering.
(1) We have illustrated a detailed phase diagram of BaFe2−xNixAs2 by x-ray and
neutron diffraction and ﬁnd a strong magneto-elastic coupling in the underdoped
regime. Furthermore, we ﬁnd that a purported quantum critical point is avoided
by the emergence of an incommensurate short-range antiferromagnetic order near
optimal doping.
(2) Because of the importance of the incommensurate order, we use various neu-
tron scattering spectrometers with different energy resolutions to study the slow
magnetic dynamics of this incommensurate order, and ﬁnd that the magnetic tran-
sition temperature TN is sensitive to instrumental energy resolution. This indicates
that the short-range incommensurate order is a short-range cluster spin glass state
coexisting and competing with superconductivity.
(3) We have discovered the nematic spin correlations using inelastic neutron scat-
tering. The similarities between the nematic spin correlations, resistivity anisotropy
and orbital ordering provide a comprehensive experimental basis for understand-
ing the origin of the electronic nematic phase in iron-based superconductors. In
addition, we have developed single-crystal detwinning techniques for large single
crystals, which will play an important role in our future studies on detwinned single
crystals of iron-based superconductors.
(4) We have investigated the doping evolution of the magnetic excitations in
overdoped BaFe2−xNixAs2 and revealed the importance of the low energy magnetic
excitations and the high energy magnetic excitations for driving superconductiv-
ity. The exchange coupling between the local moments and the itinerant electrons
that induce the low-energy spin excitations via interband scattering are two essen-
tial ingredients for creating superconductivity. This provides important clues for
understanding the origin of the magnetism, the electron correlation and the interplay
between magnetism and superconductivity in iron-based superconductors.

X. Lu, Phase Diagram and Magnetic Excitations of BaFe2−xNixAs2: A Neutron
Scattering Study, Springer Theses, DOI 10.1007/978-981-10-4998-9_8
119

120
8
Summary and Outlook
Although great progress has been made in last several years of studies of iron-
based superconductors, much remains unknown. Following what we have done, we
will focus on several important issues in this ﬁeld. Two speciﬁc issues are given
below:
(1) The nature of the magnetic excitations of BaFe2As2. It seems the magnetic
ground state and the underlying electronic interactions have been well understood.
We argue that, however, the current understanding is not complete. For example,
the high energy magnetic excitations above 200meV at Q = (1, 1) has not been
accounted in current Hamiltonian for describing the magnetic dynamics. On the
other hand, a correct Hamiltonian must be derived in describing the spin waves in
a detwinned sample, which has not been reported. We will study the spin waves of
detwinned BaFe2As2 and explain the high energy magnetic excitations by including
some non-Heisenberg interactions.
(2) The electronic nematic phase and ﬂuctuations have been well studied by resis-
tivity measurements. However, there are only several studies on the nematic spin
correlations. In the future, we will keep studying the nematic spin correlations in
iron-based superconductors exploiting creative devices and experimental techniques.
Beside these, other important and interesting topics such as quantum criticality,
spin glass state and non-Fermi liquid behavior, will also be studied, which we are
not going to discuss in detail here.
